  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/397597437?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/2329228-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=awful">awful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer397597437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1610582783834510642">Things I learned in this awful, awful Young Adult novel:<br/>1. It's okay if a freshman <i>in college</i> goes after a sophomore <i>in high school</i> if the sophomore tells him she realizes what he is up too. And if he then pronounces undying love or something equally romantic. And its totally normal for an 18 year old guy to continue being attracted to this...what? fifteen year old? if she <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ burns a hand print onto his chest.  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Because that's not creepy <i> at all</i>. <br/>2. Love, peace, harmo</span>
  <span id="freeText1610582783834510642" style="display:none">Things I learned in this awful, awful Young Adult novel:<br />1. It's okay if a freshman <i>in college</i> goes after a sophomore <i>in high school</i> if the sophomore tells him she realizes what he is up too. And if he then pronounces undying love or something equally romantic. And its totally normal for an 18 year old guy to continue being attracted to this...what? fifteen year old? if she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ burns a hand print onto his chest.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Because that's not creepy <i> at all</i>. <br />2. Love, peace, harmony....unless its applying to your older sister who likes murdering people. Granted, not the best role model in the world, but if she is going to be eaten by a creepy jelly monster and probably forfeit her life, reincarnation, and all that other fun stuff eternally, you'd think a little assistance would be in order. Forget that she just tried to murder your lame boyfriend. <i>She's your sister.</i> Get over yourself. Gosh, was I the only one who felt bad for Eve? The entire novel? Ash is a total waste of time. And her bizarre little 'death bringer' sister isn't much better. But like I was saying, its okay to live in harmony with your enemies and stuff, and murder your own. Or at least watch them get murdered. Right....that makes total sense.<br />3. Oh, and let's not forget! This is a book meant for teenagers. Got to throw in some good ole underage drinking, underage sex (technically speaking, Park Ranger Boyfriend came mighty close to legally being stuck as a sex offender for his little stunt in the bedroom), and as much language as possible. That'll get the readers.<br />4. And there are all these gods sitting around....what a perfect scenario for some potentially interesting religious discussion. Wait? No? Why not create a muddled and downright <i>confusing</i> story line where half of the mythological deities think they are the highest power possible, and the other half seem to have some... bizarre...possible....form of faith in something? Not odd at all. After all, every myth comes with its family of warring peeps. <br />5. Finally, I learned that if I read books this horrendous before going to bed, I wake up at 5 am the next morning humming heart breaker by Celtic Thunder and wanting to punch someone's lights out. Trust me, that isn't normal.<br />This book sucked, on so many levels. It <i>has</i> potential. I give you that. Some neat ideas in this plot. That's why, to my intense irritation, I kept reading. And reading. I suffer from <i>it-has-to-get-better-nothing-this-awful-would-ever-be-published</i>. But the ending was the worst part!<br />Ash is such a lame main character. She is ungrateful, irritating, hormonal, desperate....where do I end this? She didn't need to go run off with her sister Canada or wherever. She didn't need to hit the jungles of South America to find her blood thirsty torture rat little sister. But she showed no compassion no urge to help her own sister from the creepy jell men! That is what make her despicable in my eyes. <br />Every single one of the "gods/goddesses" were awful. <br />All I can say is <i>what a waste of time</i>, AVOID AVOID AVOID, and wow Anna - I admit it - I should have listened to you. <br />This book sucked.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FOiSN5QjbXu7pUYgNN1vpAvPjXZzFIepVHl301EUu1M3VI6td6FsVlcBzKCMAaKc5maV5DFEc411WOr4EAbmCg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hPd1hHYaEAjJcnYY2QHRx1U7jI7QqM13PjxRX4LLET6nS2kelZgRJSXW/Jhh3Rz/uJKUHJL4OVMfHcx0w9lMZw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7823414005083550964">Karsten Knight is the author of the historical mystery <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33887280._NIGHTINGALE__SING' title=' NIGHTINGALE, SING' rel='nofollow noopener'> NIGHTINGALE, SING</a>, the time-traveling thriller <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40020._PATCHWORK' title=' PATCHWORK' rel='nofollow noopener'> PATCHWORK</a>, and the Polynesian volcano goddess trilogy <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11478365._WILDEFIRE' title=' WILDEFIRE' rel='nofollow noopener'> WILDEFIRE</a> (Simon & Schuster)--though some say his writing career peaked at the age of six, when he completed a picture book series about an adventurous worm. He is a graduate of College of the Holy Cross and earned an MFA in writing for chil</span>
  <span id="freeText7823414005083550964" style="display:none">Karsten Knight is the author of the historical mystery <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33887280._NIGHTINGALE__SING" title=" NIGHTINGALE, SING" rel="nofollow noopener"> NIGHTINGALE, SING</a>, the time-traveling thriller <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40020._PATCHWORK" title=" PATCHWORK" rel="nofollow noopener"> PATCHWORK</a>, and the Polynesian volcano goddess trilogy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11478365._WILDEFIRE" title=" WILDEFIRE" rel="nofollow noopener"> WILDEFIRE</a> (Simon &amp; Schuster)--though some say his writing career peaked at the age of six, when he completed a picture book series about an adventurous worm. He is a graduate of College of the Holy Cross and earned an MFA in writing for children from Simmons College. Karsten resides in Boston, where he lives for fall weather, bowling, and football season. For more information on Karsten or his books, please visit <a href="www.karstenknightbooks.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.karstenknightbooks.com</a>.</span>
